<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">All enrollment figures are as of Fall 2014</td>

<p><b>Virginia Commonwealth University</b> (<b>VCU</b>) is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_education" title="Public education">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">research</a> <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond, Virginia</a>. VCU was founded in 1838 as the medical department of <a href="/wiki/Hampden%E2%80%93Sydney_College" title="Hampden–Sydney College">Hampden–Sydney College</a>, becoming the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_College_of_Virginia" title="Medical College of Virginia">Medical College of Virginia</a> in 1854. In 1968, the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">Virginia General Assembly</a> merged MCV with the <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Professional_Institute" title="Richmond Professional Institute">Richmond Professional Institute</a>, founded in 1917, to create Virginia Commonwealth University.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In 2015, more than 31,000 students pursue 226 degree and certificate programs through VCU's 13 schools and one college.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VCU_Facts_and_Rankings_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-VCU_Facts_and_Rankings-3">[3]</a></sup> The VCU Health System supports the university's health care education, research and patient care mission.</p>
<p>With a record $270.3 million in sponsored research funding in the fiscal year 2014–15, VCU is designated as "R1: Doctoral University - Highest Research Activity" by the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-facts-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> A broad array of university-approved centers and institutes of excellence, involving faculty from multiple disciplines in public policy, biotechnology and health care discoveries, supports the university's research mission. Twenty-eight graduate and first-professional programs are ranked by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> as among the best in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> VCU's athletic teams compete in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> and are collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/VCU_Rams" title="VCU Rams">VCU Rams</a>. They are members of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">Atlantic 10 Conference</a>. The VCU campus includes historic buildings such as the <a href="/wiki/Ginter_House" title="Ginter House">Ginter House</a>, now used by the school's <a href="/wiki/Provost_(education)" title="Provost (education)">provost</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="History of Virginia Commonwealth University">History of Virginia Commonwealth University</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_presidents_of_Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="List of presidents of Virginia Commonwealth University">List of presidents of Virginia Commonwealth University</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings">Beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Egyptian_Building.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Egyptian_Building.JPG/400px-Egyptian_Building.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Egyptian_Building.JPG/600px-Egyptian_Building.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Egyptian_Building.JPG/800px-Egyptian_Building.JPG 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Egyptian_Building.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Building" title="Egyptian Building">Egyptian Building</a> of the Medical College of Virginia (1845), Richmond, Virginia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Though officially created with the merger of the <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Professional_Institute" title="Richmond Professional Institute">Richmond Professional Institute</a> (RPI) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_College_of_Virginia" title="Medical College of Virginia">Medical College of Virginia</a> (MCV) in 1968, VCU's history began in 1838 when the Medical Department of Hampden-Sydney College opened in Richmond. In 1844, it moved into its first permanent home, the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Building" title="Egyptian Building">Egyptian Building</a>. In 1854, the Medical Department of Hampden–Sydney College received an independent charter from the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">Virginia General Assembly</a> and became the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_College_of_Virginia" title="Medical College of Virginia">Medical College of Virginia</a></i> (MCV). A few years later in 1860, MCV conveyed all its property to the Commonwealth of Virginia and becomes a state institution in exchange for $30,000. In 1893, the College of Physicians and Surgeons, later University College of Medicine, was established by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunter_Holmes_McGuire" title="Hunter Holmes McGuire">Hunter Holmes McGuire</a> just three blocks away from MCV. In 1912, McGuire Hall opened as the new home of the University College of Medicine. The following year, MCV and UCM merged through the efforts of George Ben Johnston and Stuart McGuire. MCV acquired the Memorial Hospital as a result of the merger.</p>
<p>Richmond Professional Institute traces its roots back to 1917, when it began as the Richmond School of Social Work and Public Health. In 1925, it became the Richmond division of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_College_of_William_%26_Mary" title="The College of William &amp; Mary">The College of William &amp; Mary</a>. In 1939, this division became the <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Professional_Institute" title="Richmond Professional Institute">Richmond Professional Institute</a> of The College of William &amp; Mary" (RPI). In 1947, the MCV Foundation was incorporated, and in 1962 RPI separated from William &amp; Mary to become an independent state institution. Then in 1968, state legislation (Wayne Commission Report) merged MCV and RPI to become Virginia Commonwealth University. VCU claims 1838 as its founding date on its official seal and on promotional materials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-History-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, VCU was awarded a $62 million federal grant to oversee a national research consortium of universities, hospitals and clinics to study what happens to service members and veterans who suffer mild traumatic brain injuries or concussions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, VCU received a $20 million National Institutes of Health grant to join a nationwide consortium of research institutions working to turn laboratory discoveries into treatments for patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-12">[12]</a></sup> The Clinical and Translational Science Award made VCU the only academic health center in Virginia to join the prestigious CTSA network. In 2011, The Carnegie Foundation elevated Virginia Commonwealth University to "Very High Research Activity," with over 255 million in sponsored research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Rao" title="Michael Rao">Michael Rao</a> was appointed the fifth president of VCU and continues in his tenure to focus on VCU's growth as a premier public research university.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_at_VCU">Expansion at VCU</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Expansion at VCU">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VCU_expansion" title="VCU expansion">VCU expansion</a></div>
<p>Warren W. Brandt served as the first president of VCU. During his tenure, 32 degree programs were added, and the School of Allied Health Professions and the School of Community Services were established. In addition, more than $20 million of new construction was completed or initiated on both campuses, including the <a href="/wiki/James_Branch_Cabell" title="James Branch Cabell">James Branch Cabell</a> Library, Rhoads Hall, the School of Business building, the Larrick Student Center and a large addition to Sanger Hall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-History-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1980s, and under the leadership of VCU President Edmund Ackell, a major overhaul of the university's governance system and administrative structure was initiated. Dr. Ackell lead the administration in instituting a new system for both short-range and long-range university planning; establishing faculty convocation and a new set of faculty tenure and promotion guidelines; and establishing greater access to the community by supporting the use of the university's research and educational resources to meet social needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-History-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eugene_Trani" title="Eugene Trani">Eugene Trani</a> became the president of VCU in 1990. During his tenure VCU became one of the largest universities in Virginia, growing from an enrollment of 21,764 in 1990, to 32,284 at the time of his retirement. VCU was the state's first university to enroll over 30,000 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Under Dr. Trani's leadership VCU and the VCU Health System undertook more than $2.2 billion in capital construction and renovation projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> In February 2006, VCU established VCU 2020 Vision for Excellence, a strategic plan to continue to fulfill VCU's mission as a leading urban research institution for the 21st century and develop more than $1 billion in new academic, medical, recreation, student housing, and parking facilities on VCU's Monroe Park and MCV Campuses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.vcu.edu_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-news.vcu.edu-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="VCU_Quest_for_Distinction">VCU Quest for Distinction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: VCU Quest for Distinction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Quest for Distinction, the university's strategic plan, was launched by Dr. Rao in 2011. It sets priorities of academic excellence, research that enhances the quality of life, human health and well-being, and ongoing contribution to the economic vitality and cultural richness of the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Specific initiatives include the continued recruitment of high-quality faculty and resource development aimed at enhancing the overall student experience. The latest master plan lays out over 3 billion dollars in new construction and renovations that would provide housing for an additional 1,300 students, increase parking for several thousand cars and build 3 million additional square feet of academic and research space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Virginia Commonwealth University has two main campuses in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond,_Va." title="Richmond, Va.">Richmond, Va.</a>: the Monroe Park Campus, located west of downtown Richmond, and the MCV Campus in the urban center. Additionally, VCU has a branch campus in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Education_City,_Qatar" title="Education City, Qatar">Education City, Qatar</a>, along with numerous regional facilities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monroe_Park_Campus">Monroe Park Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Monroe Park Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VCU_Snead_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/VCU_Snead_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG/350px-VCU_Snead_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/VCU_Snead_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG/525px-VCU_Snead_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/VCU_Snead_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG/700px-VCU_Snead_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VCU_Snead_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Snead Hall, Monroe Park campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Named after the city park, the 90.6-acre Monroe Park Campus took its name in June 2004, replacing the former name, the Academic Campus of VCU. The Monroe Park Campus houses most of VCU's general education facilities, and is situated on the eastern end of the <a href="/wiki/Fan_district" title="Fan district">Fan district</a>, a historic, late 19th-century neighborhood adjacent to downtown Richmond. Prior to the merger of the <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Professional_Institute" title="Richmond Professional Institute">Richmond Professional Institute</a> and the Medical College of Virginia, the campus was the home to the entire Richmond Professional Institute. Today, the campus has a mixture of modern and vintage buildings, with over 40 structures built before 1900.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="MCV_Campus">MCV Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: MCV Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VCU_Medical_Science_Building_2_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" height="448" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/VCU_Medical_Science_Building_2_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg/300px-VCU_Medical_Science_Building_2_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/VCU_Medical_Science_Building_2_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg/450px-VCU_Medical_Science_Building_2_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/VCU_Medical_Science_Building_2_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg/600px-VCU_Medical_Science_Building_2_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VCU_Medical_Science_Building_2_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
VCU Molecular Medicine Research Building (MMRB), MCV campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 52.3-acre MCV Campus is home to the <a href="/wiki/VCU_Medical_Center" title="VCU Medical Center">VCU Medical Center</a>. This includes the Schools of Medicine, Dentistry, Pharmacy, Allied Health, Nursing, and the medical center, which is overseen by the VCU Health System Authority. The campus is also home to the <a href="/wiki/VCU_Massey_Cancer_Center" title="VCU Massey Cancer Center">Massey Cancer Center</a> (an <a href="/wiki/NCI-designated_Cancer_Center" title="NCI-designated Cancer Center">NCI-designated Cancer Center</a>) and the Children's Hospital of Richmond at VCU. The MCV Campus is an integral part of Richmond in the old <a href="/wiki/Court_End" title="Court End">Court End</a> district. The neighborhood is located adjacent to the city's business and financial district near the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Capitol" title="Virginia State Capitol">state capitol</a>. VCU's Health Sciences schools comprise the <a href="/wiki/VCU_School_of_Allied_Health_Professions" title="VCU School of Allied Health Professions">School of Allied Health Professions</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University_School_of_Dentistry" title="Virginia Commonwealth University School of Dentistry">School of Dentistry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/VCU_School_of_Medicine" title="VCU School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/VCU_School_of_Nursing" title="VCU School of Nursing">School of Nursing</a>, and the School of Pharmacy.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="VCUQatar">VCUQatar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: VCUQatar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University_-_Qatar" title="Virginia Commonwealth University - Qatar">Virginia Commonwealth University - Qatar</a></div>
<p>VCUQatar (VCUQ) is VCU School of the Arts' branch campus located in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Qatar" title="State of Qatar">State of Qatar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>VCUQ is the Qatar campus of the Virginia Commonwealth University School of the Arts in Richmond, Virginia. It was established in 1998 through a partnership with Qatar Foundation and was the first university to open its doors in Education City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The contract was renewed in July 2012 and goes through July 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-23">[23]</a></sup> VCUQ provides students the opportunity to earn a Bachelor of Fine Arts degree in Graphic Design, Interior Design, Fashion Design, Art History, or Painting and Printmaking and a Master of Fine Arts degree in Design Studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> As part of the contract, VCU is not allowed to open any other degree-granting arts or design programs in other Middle Eastern countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to smart classrooms, the VCUQ campus is primarily composed of studios and workspaces for its art programs, an international gallery and a library. The campus also contains things needed for daily student life such as a café, prayer rooms, a student lounge, and a central hall which can be used for a variety of events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Through its programs, VCUQatar's mission is to "develop the individual capacity to lead innovations in the creative and cultural professions in Qatar and the region."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>VCUQ is accredited by National Association of Schools of Art &amp; Design, The Southern Association of Colleges and Schools and Council for Interior Design Accreditation.</p>
<p>In 2010, VCUQatar more than doubled its facilities through a major expansion project. The expansion has allowed for the integration of the university's undergraduate and graduate programs under one roof, the connection of the research and entrepreneurship offices with curricular programs, and the expansion of technical spaces to support all forms of visualization and research with a media lab, digital fabrication lab, printmaking studios, photography studio, an expanded library and the first materials library in the region.</p>
<p>The campus is working alongside the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Supreme_Education_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Supreme Education Council (page does not exist)">Supreme Education Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Foundation" title="Qatar Foundation">Qatar Foundation</a> toward reaching the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_National_Vision_2030" title="Qatar National Vision 2030">Qatar National Vision 2030</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, VCUQatar has 66 Faculty representing for 15 diffrrent nationalities. The number of students is 282 Students representing 40 nationalities which shows its diversity. So far VCUQatar has 450 Alumni representing 33 nationalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> VCU received about $42 million in 2014 to operate the campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> A portion of this is a management fee, which in previous years was $3.4 million, allowing the campus to profit off of the campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-23">[23]</a></sup> VCU is not the only US campus in Education City, and it, along with the other universities, are the subject of criticism of their implicit acceptance of Qatar's sponsorship of terrorism and egregious human rights violations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="VCU_satellite_and_research_locations">VCU satellite and research locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: VCU satellite and research locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Virginia Bio-Technology Research Park was incorporated in May 1992 as a joint initiative of Virginia Commonwealth University (VCU), the City of Richmond and the Commonwealth of Virginia. The research park is home to more than 60 life science companies, research institutes and state/federal labs, employing more than 2,200 scientists, engineers and researchers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li>Inger and Walter Rice Center for Environmental Life Sciences is located on 494 acres along the <a href="/wiki/James_River" title="James River">James River</a>. The center has a primary focus of research on the science and policy of large rivers and their fringing riparian and wetland landscapes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li>VCU Medical Center at Stony Point, in southwestern Richmond<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
<li>VCU School of Medicine Inova Campus<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li>VCU School of Pharmacy Inova Campus<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>VCU School of Pharmacy University of Virginia Division<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Programs">Programs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Programs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>VCU offers <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">Baccalaureate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">Master's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">Doctoral</a> <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">degrees</a>, as well as Professional and Certificate courses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Seventy-nine of VCU's programs are unique to Virginia, such as the Homeland Security and Emergency Preparedness major in the L. Douglas Wilder School of Government and Public Affairs, as well as the Real Estate and Urban Land Development degree in VCU's School of Business. The university also offers a wide range of study options with 225 certificate, undergraduate, graduate, professional and doctoral degrees in the arts, sciences and humanities.</p>
<p>The university's medical campus provides students with several opportunities for postgraduate study. Under the Guaranteed Admission Program,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-honors.vcu.edu_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-honors.vcu.edu-59">[59]</a></sup> select incoming undergraduates who maintain a high academic standard are guaranteed a spot in a number of professional health science programs.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="VCU_Living-Learning_programs">VCU Living-Learning programs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: VCU Living-Learning programs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>VCU's Academic Scholars Program in Real Environments (ASPiRE),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> combines the living-learning experience with community engagement. Launched in fall 2012, VCU ASPiRE links students with their community and with each other through a coordinated educational and service-learning curriculum and living experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>The VCU Honors College<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> is available to students meeting specific SAT/ACT and GPA criteria. Through the Honors College eligible students are offered the Guaranteed Admission Program,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-honors.vcu.edu_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-honors.vcu.edu-59">[59]</a></sup> which offers a variety of options for gaining early admission into the professional health science and graduate programs at VCU. In addition, the Honors College also offers students the ability to enroll in classes open only to honors students, live in honors-only residence halls, apply for scholarships only available to honors students, and participate in The Honors College Mentorship Program and other learning experiences that supplement general classroom study.</p>
<p>VCU Globe prepares undergraduates to live and work in a global environment, expanding students' identities as global citizens through course work, co-curricular activities and the residential experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>VCU LEAD is focused on developing graduates who can successfully lead professional and civic organizations at a local, national, and global level within their respective fields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>VCU Innovate is to spur a mindset and cross-disciplinary culture that enables students to pursue innovation and entrepreneurship efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_Sciences">Life Sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Life Sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>VCU Life Sciences<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> comprises three units: the Center for the Study of Biological Complexity (CSBC), the Center for Environmental Studies (CES), and the Rice Center for Environmental Life Sciences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> VCU Life Sciences offers an undergraduate and graduate programs as well as a PhD program in Integrated Life Sciences (ILS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Note that the Department of Biology<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> is a separate unit independent of Life Sciences although there are numerous active interactions between the two. The highly interdisciplinary, systems-based program relies on hundreds of faculty members. With activities at the local, regional and national levels, VCU Life Sciences helps increase public literacy in the life sciences and provides an assessment of American public attitudes toward the field.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="VCU_da_Vinci_Center">VCU da Vinci Center</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: VCU da Vinci Center">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>VCU schools of the Arts, Business, and Engineering have collaborated to create the VCU da Vinci Center for Innovation in Product Design and Development. Student teams from these schools take on a product development or design challenge posed by one of the Center's industry partners. Such cross-disciplinary educational opportunities prepare students for management roles in the global, technology-driven workplace of the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> In addition to the current collaboration, the College of Humanities and Sciences<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> joined the Center late in the fall 2012 semester. The VCU da Vinci Center currently offers an Undergraduate Certificate and a master's degree in Product Innovation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The Masters of Product Innovation is the first of its kind in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The center was recognized by a report presented to <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">President Obama</a> as one of the 29 best programs to offer a STEM (science, technology, engineering, and math) degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-74">[74]</a></sup> It was the only program in Virginia to be included on the list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="VCU's_International_Partnership_Universities_Initiative"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="VCU.27s_International_Partnership_Universities_Initiative">VCU's International Partnership Universities Initiative</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: VCU's International Partnership Universities Initiative">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>VCU's International Partnership Universities Initiative provides faculty and students the opportunity for involvement and collaboration in an international and multicultural arena. Fifteen international Partnership Universities and VCU School in Qatar are strategically located in 11 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bauhaus_University,_Weimar" title="Bauhaus University, Weimar">Bauhaus University, Weimar</a> (Germany)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beijing_Foreign_Studies_University" title="Beijing Foreign Studies University">Beijing Foreign Studies University</a> (China)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Curtin_University" title="Curtin University">Curtin University of Technology</a> (Australia)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fudan_University" title="Fudan University">Fudan University</a> (China)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hadassah_Medical_Center" title="Hadassah Medical Center">Hadassah Medical Center</a> (Israel)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harris_Manchester_College,_Oxford" title="Harris Manchester College, Oxford">Harris Manchester College</a> (United Kingdom)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Indian_Institutes_of_Technology" title="Indian Institutes of Technology">Indian Institute of Technology</a> (India)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxford_University" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a> (United Kingdom)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post_Graduate_Institute_of_Medical_Education_and_Research" title="Post Graduate Institute of Medical Education and Research">Post Graduate Institute of Medical Education and Research</a> (India)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_University" title="Moscow State University">Moscow State University</a> (Russia)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_State_University" title="Saint Petersburg State University">St. Petersburg State University</a> (Russia)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_C%C3%B3rdoba_(Spain)" title="University of Córdoba (Spain)">University of Córdoba (Spain)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Guadalajara" title="University of Guadalajara">University of Guadalajara</a> (Mexico)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_KwaZulu-Natal" title="University of KwaZulu-Natal">University of KwaZulu–Natal</a> (South Africa)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Messina" title="University of Messina">University of Messina</a> (Italy)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="University of São Paulo">University of São Paulo</a> (Brazil)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_of_England" title="University of the West of England">University of the West of England</a> (United Kingdom)</li>
</ul>

<p>According to the 2016 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>, VCU is classified as a Tier 1 University with an overall National University rank of No. 156 and holds a rank of No. 84 among all public colleges and universities in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> conducted in 2005 by the Institute of Higher Education at <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a> ranks VCU in the top 100 universities in North &amp; Latin America and one of the top 200 universities in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Virginia Commonwealth University School of the Arts (VCUarts) is ranked the No. 1 public university school of arts and design in the country (#4 among public &amp; private institutions) by <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> in 2015.<sup>[Out of Date]</sup> VCUarts is the only public university arts and design school in the country to ever be ranked this high in overall ranking. Indeed, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> called it "that rare public research institution that has put the arts front and center".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/VCU_Brandcenter" title="VCU Brandcenter">VCU Brandcenter</a>, the School of Business' graduate program in advertising, has also been ranked first in the nation by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Creativity_Magazine" title="Creativity Magazine">Creativity Magazine</a></i> and as one of the top 60 design schools in the world by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek">BusinessWeek</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup>[Out of Date]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:377px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VCU_Fine_Arts_Building_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/VCU_Fine_Arts_Building_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG/375px-VCU_Fine_Arts_Building_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/VCU_Fine_Arts_Building_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG/563px-VCU_Fine_Arts_Building_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/VCU_Fine_Arts_Building_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG/750px-VCU_Fine_Arts_Building_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG 2x" width="375"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VCU_Fine_Arts_Building_by_Jeff_Auth.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Fine Arts Building, Monroe Park Campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>VCU's <a class="external text" href="http://had.vcu.edu/programs/msha/index.html" rel="nofollow">Masters of Science in Health Administration</a> program was ranked second by Modern Healthcare. The University's Health System earned national Magnet nursing designation by the American Nurses Credentialing Center, and has twice been named one of the Solucient Top 100 Hospitals in the United States by Solucient Corporation. In research the school has been ranked as a top American university by Lombardi Program on Measuring University Performance and a top 100 university by the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>. VCU Engineering, started in 1996 has seen tremendous growth and completely new facilities. William F. Goodwin, Chairman of the VCU School of Engineering Foundation Board of Trustees, has set an ambitious objective for the engineering program. He's aiming for "25 in 25" – a top 25 engineering-school rank within 25 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> As of 2014, U.S News &amp; Report ranks the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomedical_Engineering" title="Biomedical Engineering">Biomedical Engineering</a> program 58th, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_Engineering" title="Computer Engineering">Computer Engineering</a> program 84th, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Electrical/Electronic/Communications_Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Electrical/Electronic/Communications Engineering (page does not exist)">Electrical/Electronic/Communications Engineering</a> 89th in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The School of Business currently ranks as the No. 51 part-time MBA program and No. 97 best undergraduate business program in the United States according to <i>Bloomberg Businessweek</i> and <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i>, respectively.</p>
<p>According to the 2012 <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> <a class="external text" href="http://www.socialwork.vcu.edu" rel="nofollow">VCU School of Social Work</a> is ranked 11<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> and the Public Affairs graduate program is currently ranked 53 in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The VCU SportsCenter is a graduate program offering a master's degree in Sports Leadership. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=David_Maraghy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="David Maraghy (page does not exist)">David Maraghy</a> co-founded and served as Executive Director of the program until 2002. It is currently directed by Nathan Tomasini. One of the program's elite events is known as Villa 7 which began as a forum where athletic directors could share ideas and meet with the country's elite assistant basketball coaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>VCU is among the top 100 institutions according to the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> rankings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In its history, one faculty member and one alumnus have won a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>: <b><a href="/wiki/Baruj_Benacerraf" title="Baruj Benacerraf">Baruj Benacerraf</a></b>, an alumnus of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_College_of_Virginia" title="Medical College of Virginia">Medical College of Virginia</a>, was awarded the 1980 Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine, and <a href="/wiki/John_Fenn_(chemist)" title="John Fenn (chemist)"><b>John Fenn</b></a>, a professor in the College of Humanities &amp; Sciences, was awarded the 2002 Nobel Prize in Chemistry.</p>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VCU_commons.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
VCU Student Commons, Monroe Park Campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the medical field, VCU has had four professors elected to the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a>, most recently <b>Steven Woolf</b> in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>Historically, notable faculty members include <b><a href="/wiki/Charles-%C3%89douard_Brown-S%C3%A9quard" title="Charles-Édouard Brown-Séquard">Charles-Édouard Brown-Séquard</a></b>, M.D., for whom <a href="/wiki/Brown-S%C3%A9quard_syndrome" title="Brown-Séquard syndrome">Brown-Séquard syndrome</a> is named. <b><a href="/wiki/Hunter_McGuire" title="Hunter McGuire">Hunter McGuire</a></b>, M.D., was the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate</a> surgeon for General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_J._%22Stonewall%22_Jackson" title='Thomas J. "Stonewall" Jackson'>Thomas J. "Stonewall" Jackson</a> before he founded the "University College of Medicine", which later merged with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_College_of_Virginia" title="Medical College of Virginia">Medical College of Virginia</a> where he became the Chairman of Surgery. The <a href="/wiki/Hunter_Holmes_McGuire_Veterans_Administration_Medical_Center" title="Hunter Holmes McGuire Veterans Administration Medical Center">Hunter Holmes McGuire Veterans Administration Medical Center</a> is named in his honor.</p>
<p><b>Jennifer Johnson</b>'s (Professor of Sociology) work at the Department of Defense in the area of Social Network Analysis won her the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff_Joint_Distinguished_Civilian_Service_Award" title="Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff Joint Distinguished Civilian Service Award">Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff Joint Distinguished Civilian Service Award</a>, which is the highest-ranking civilian service award given by the Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff. Dr. Johnson was also awarded the 2004 Analyst of the Quarter by the Joint Warfare Analysis Center for her work on the Social Network Analysis Methodology Team. Also <b><a href="/wiki/Gevork_Minaskanian" title="Gevork Minaskanian">Gevork Minaskanian</a></b>, cofounder of Aderis Pharmaceuticals, developers of <a href="/wiki/Rotigotine" title="Rotigotine">Rotigotine</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Dopamine_agonist" title="Dopamine agonist">dopamine agonist</a> for treatment of <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson's disease">Parkinson's disease</a>, teaches at VCU.</p>
<p>The VCU Counseling Psychology Graduate Program was ranked 3rd in the nation in the Faculty Scholarly Productivity Index in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The VCU Public Administration program in the L. Douglas Wilder School for Government and Public Affairs was ranked 9th in the nation by the Faculty Scholarly Productivity Index in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:James_Branch_Cabell_Library_VCU.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/James_Branch_Cabell_Library_VCU.jpg/400px-James_Branch_Cabell_Library_VCU.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/James_Branch_Cabell_Library_VCU.jpg/600px-James_Branch_Cabell_Library_VCU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/James_Branch_Cabell_Library_VCU.jpg/800px-James_Branch_Cabell_Library_VCU.jpg 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:James_Branch_Cabell_Library_VCU.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
James Branch Cabell Library, Monroe Park Campus, prior to 2015 renovation.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="external text" href="http://library.vcu.edu" rel="nofollow">VCU Libraries</a> is one of the largest research libraries in Virginia. The libraries hold more than 2.58 million volumes (including more than 665,000 electronic books) and extensive journal and database holdings. Collection strengths include the arts, behavioral sciences, business, chemistry, clinical medicine, education, health and life sciences, public affairs, and social work. The VCU Libraries hosts 2.16 million visitors each year.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/James_Branch_Cabell" title="James Branch Cabell">James Branch Cabell</a> Library supports the Monroe Park Campus. Its <a class="external text" href="http://www.library.vcu.edu/research/special-collections/cabell/" rel="nofollow">Special Collections and Archives department</a> houses one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Artist%27s_book" title="Artist's book">book art</a> collections in the Southeast and the fifth largest <a href="/wiki/Graphic_novel" title="Graphic novel">graphic novel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">comic book</a> collections in the United States. It also includes records of local organizations and papers of numerous Virginia writers, artists, and social activists from Virginia's under-documented communities, and is the repository of the <a href="/wiki/Eisner_Award" title="Eisner Award">Will Eisner Comic Industry Awards</a>. In early 2016, VCU Libraries acquired a rare copy of <a href="/wiki/All-Negro_Comics" title="All-Negro Comics">All-Negro Comics</a> No. 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="external text" href="http://www.library.vcu.edu/about/libraries/tompkins-mccaw/" rel="nofollow">Tompkins–McCaw Library for the Health Sciences</a> on the MCV Campus has the largest medical collection in the state, with extensive journal collections dating back to the nineteenth century. Special collections maintain the papers of health care practitioners and the history of health care in Virginia. Its Medical Artifacts Collection has more than 6,000 instruments and equipment related to the history of health care in Virginia over the last 150 years.</p>
<p>In March 2016, a 93,000-square-foot expansion of Cabell Library was dedicated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The new space has allowed for the addition of a multimedia production suite, a maker-space, and 25 study rooms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Ninety percent of the additional space has been dedicated to student and researcher use rather than staff offices or book storage.</p>
<p>The VCU Libraries offers electronic access to some of its special collections, including papers, images, and sound files relating to civil rights, Richmond architecture, civil war medicine, comic-book and cartooning arts, medical artifacts, and the history of VCU.</p>
<p>Library initiatives have included the 2014 Freedom Now Project,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> which published civil rights protests in 1963 <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_County,_Virginia" title="Prince Edward County, Virginia">Prince Edward County, Virginia</a> and invited citizens to come forward to help identify participants and tell these untold stories. In 2015, a 19th-century map overlaid with current geospacial data and Google maps allowed researchers and the public to explore the history and architecture of Richmond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The student body consists of 57% female students and 42% male students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Out-of-state students have increased to 15% as of the fall of 2011, and the remaining 85% of students are from Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opds.vcu.edu_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-opds.vcu.edu-4">[4]</a></sup> Demographically, the student body is 51% white, 15% African American, 12% Asian, 7% Hispanic, 6% International, less than 1% Native American and 8% Unknown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VCU_Facts_and_Rankings_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-VCU_Facts_and_Rankings-3">[3]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residential_life">Residential life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Residential life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VCU_Brandt_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/VCU_Brandt_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg/170px-VCU_Brandt_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/VCU_Brandt_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg/255px-VCU_Brandt_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/VCU_Brandt_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg/340px-VCU_Brandt_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VCU_Brandt_Hall_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brandt Hall, Monroe Park Campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Housing_at_Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Housing at Virginia Commonwealth University">Housing at Virginia Commonwealth University</a></div>
<p>More than 79% of VCU freshmen live on campus. VCU's current residential hall capacity is around 5,400 students, but will have a capacity of around 5,800 students by 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Because of the prominent location within the city of Richmond, many upperclassmen live in student apartments located around the campus, specifically in <a href="/wiki/Fan_district" title="Fan district">The Fan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Hill" title="Oregon Hill">Oregon Hill</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Carver,_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Carver, Richmond, Virginia">Carver</a> neighborhood, and are still able to walk or bike to their classes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VCU_Shafer_Dining_Center_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/VCU_Shafer_Dining_Center_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg/220px-VCU_Shafer_Dining_Center_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/VCU_Shafer_Dining_Center_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg/330px-VCU_Shafer_Dining_Center_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/VCU_Shafer_Dining_Center_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg/440px-VCU_Shafer_Dining_Center_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VCU_Shafer_Dining_Center_by_Jeff_Auth.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shafer Court Dining Center, Monroe Park campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dining">Dining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Dining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dining Services at VCU is contracted to ARAMARK Higher Education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Undergraduate students living in a dorm-style university residence hall are required to purchase a residential dining plan. VCU Dining Services offers a variety of plans that allow a specific number of "Swipes" and "Dining Dollars"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> to be used throughout a semester. All unused swipes and dining dollars are forfeited at the end of each semester. "Swipes" are described as the equivalent of one-meal. Swipes can be used to enter Shafer Court Dining Center, the buffet style dining hall, and through swipe exchanges at various VCU retail restaurants during specific times. "Dining Dollars" allow students the opportunity to purchase tax-free meals at any VCU retail restaurant. Commuter students, students living off campus, faculty, and staff have the option of purchasing a nonresidential dining plan. Many dining options are available at restaurants not affiliated with VCU within a short walking distance. Chipotle, Panera Bread, Domino's, Papa John's and Five Guys are some of the most popular ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities">Activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Student organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>VCU has more than 500 registered student organizations in which students can be involved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> VCU boasts a well-established net of ethnic and cultural, religious, recreational and special interest organizations. There are two student government associations at VCU, one for each campus.</p>
<p>VCU is also an academic partner to the largest <a href="/wiki/VCU_French_Film_Festival" title="VCU French Film Festival">French Film Festival</a> in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frenchfilm.vcu.edu_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-frenchfilm.vcu.edu-112">[112]</a></sup> Founded in 1993, the total participation in 2012 has grown to more than 22,000 entries for the 27 films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frenchfilm.vcu.edu_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-frenchfilm.vcu.edu-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_media">Student media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Student media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>VCU offers many student-run media outlets that allow students to express themselves without censorship or administrative control. See more at www.vcustudentmedia.com.</p>
<ul>
<li>Amendment - An annual literary journal that presents points of view outside mainstream culture, specializing in social progression through artistic expression.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Commonwealth_Times" title="The Commonwealth Times">The Commonwealth Times</a></i> – An independent student-run and -written newspaper published once a week during the school year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a class="external text" href="http://issuu.com/ink_magazine" rel="nofollow">Ink Magazine</a></i> – Multi-ethnic student news magazine published two times during the academic year, an publishes online year round.</li>
<li>"Poictesme" – An undergraduate student literary journal distributed every spring to the student body and surrounding community<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li>Potboiler Podcast Network - a network of podcasts. www.potboilervcu.com</li>
<li><i>Rams Review</i> – A student-run sports media outlet<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WVCW" title="WVCW">WVCW</a> – A student-run independent radio station at VCU<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>The Horn</i> – An inactive student-run multimedia website about the local music scene in Richmond<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreational_sports">Recreational sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Recreational sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Recreational Sports<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> offers facilities on both campuses. Opened in spring 2010, the newly renovated Cary Street Gym<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> includes the 18,000-square-foot fitness center, a rock climbing wall, two pools, racquetball and basketball courts, a track and an aerobics mezzanine.</p>
<p>The MCV Campus Recreation and Aquatic Center provide space for basketball, volleyball, racquetball and other sports. A 25-meter, six-lane pool is available for lap swimming, water basketball and volleyball. Outing Rental Center offers equipment such as backpacks, sleeping bags, tents and canoes as well as books, maps, videos and trail guides at affordable rental rates.</p>
<p>The VCU Outdoor Adventure Program<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> provides a full schedule of day trips and weekend excursions focused on such outdoor activities as camping, kayaking, white-water rafting, canoeing and caving.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Service_learning">Service learning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Service learning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Service learning at VCU is a course-based, credit-bearing educational experience in which students participate in an organized service activity that meets community-identified needs. More than 3,000 VCU students are enrolled in service learning at VCU.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_system">Greek system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Greek system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Virginia Commonwealth University hosts 36 international fraternities and sororities across four governing councils with over 1,700 students. Within the student body, a total of 6.3% of women join a sorority and 8% of men join a fraternity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> VCU's fraternity and sorority community has grown particularly rapidly in the last few years. .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commonwealthtimes.org_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-commonwealthtimes.org-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
