<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>VCU's police force consists of 99 sworn police officers and more than 200 security personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> VCU also provides a free Security Escort service (RAM SAFE) to students and faculty to assist them in reaching their destination and have stationed more than 370 Emergency Reporting Telephone Systems in various areas throughout campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/VCU_Rams" title="VCU Rams">VCU Rams</a></div>
<p>Having competed at the NCAA Division I level for little more than 30 years, Virginia Commonwealth University has sponsored a broad-based program of intercollegiate athletics. The VCU Rams have won in excess of 30 conference championships, participated in numerous NCAA post-season championship events, including a run to the Final Four in men's basketball in 2011, and had a number of All-Americans—both academic and athletic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> VCU currently sponsors sixteen varsity teams in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> Division I play through the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">Atlantic 10 Conference</a> (A10).</p>
<p>VCU Men's tennis is one of the school's most successful programs. The team is coached by Paul Kostin who is one of five Division I coaches to reach the 900-victory mark. The Men's tennis team holds 12 CAA Championships, 18 NCAA tournament appearances, and 17 years of finishing in the top 25 rankings in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> In 2000, VCU men's tennis had its best season, finishing runner up to Stanford in the NCAA Finals Championship match. The team finished with a No. 9 ranking in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also under coach Paul Kostin, VCU's women's tennis team has 3 CAA championships, 12 NCAA appearances, and 8 years in the top 25.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/VCU_Rams_baseball" title="VCU Rams baseball">VCU Baseball</a> has won a total of 3 CAA Championships and has been to a total of 8 NCAA Regionals. VCU Baseball's head coach is Shawn Stiffler, and games are played at <a href="/wiki/The_Diamond_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="The Diamond (Richmond, Virginia)">The Diamond (Richmond, Virginia)</a>.</p>
<p>Other intercollegiate sports include Men and Women's Basketball, Men and Women's Cross Country, Field Hockey, Golf, Men and Women's Soccer (played at <a href="/wiki/Sports_Backers_Stadium" title="Sports Backers Stadium">Sports Backers Stadium</a>), Men and Women's Track and Field, Volleyball, and Women's Lacrosse.</p>
<p>VCU also has many student run club teams. These sports not sponsored by the university include coed &amp; allgirl cheerleading, baseball, softball, men's<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> and women's<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_(sport)" title="Ultimate (sport)">ultimate</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a>, cycling, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Men%27s_and_women%27s_crew&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Men's and women's crew (page does not exist)">men's and women's crew</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> and dodgeball. Previous club sports have also included wrestling and tennis.</p>
<h3><span id="VCU_Rams_men's_basketball"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="VCU_Rams_men.27s_basketball">VCU Rams men's basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: VCU Rams men's basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Interior_stuart_c_siegel_center_VCU_richmond_VA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Interior_stuart_c_siegel_center_VCU_richmond_VA.jpg/275px-Interior_stuart_c_siegel_center_VCU_richmond_VA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Interior_stuart_c_siegel_center_VCU_richmond_VA.jpg/413px-Interior_stuart_c_siegel_center_VCU_richmond_VA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Interior_stuart_c_siegel_center_VCU_richmond_VA.jpg/550px-Interior_stuart_c_siegel_center_VCU_richmond_VA.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Interior_stuart_c_siegel_center_VCU_richmond_VA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The interior of the Verizon Wireless Arena within the Siegel Center, home court of the VCU basketball teams</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/VCU_Rams_men%27s_basketball" title="VCU Rams men's basketball">VCU Rams men's basketball</a></div>
<p>VCU reached the Final Four in the 2011 NCAA tournament. The team has won a total of 9 conference championships with the most recent coming in 2015, the team's first A10 championship win. The VCU Rams currently play at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stuart_C._Siegel_Center" title="Stuart C. Siegel Center">Stuart C. Siegel Center</a>, where they hold the 11th highest Home Court winning percentage in Division I basketball with a winning percentage of .8579<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="2011 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">2011 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_VCU_Rams_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 VCU Rams men's basketball team">VCU</a> qualified as an at-large bid, having to play in the newly formatted tournament's "First Four" against <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_USC_Trojans_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 USC Trojans men's basketball team">USC</a>. The decision to allow VCU to participate in the tournament was widely criticized among pundits and the media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> VCU defeated USC 59–46 in the "First Four" play-in game. VCU then went on to upset <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">Georgetown</a> 74–56 in the round of 64. The 11th-seeded VCU Rams then upset 3rd-seeded <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Purdue_Boilermakers_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 Purdue Boilermakers men's basketball team">Purdue</a> 94–76 to advance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship#Regional_semifinals_and_finals" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">Sweet 16</a> for the first time in school history. In the sweet sixteen, VCU defeated 10th-seeded <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Florida_State_Seminoles_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 Florida State Seminoles men's basketball team">Florida State</a> 72–71 on a last second bucket in overtime to advance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elite_8" title="Elite 8">Elite 8</a> for the first time in school history. VCU beat the No. 1 seed <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Kansas_Jayhawks_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 Kansas Jayhawks men's basketball team">Kansas</a> in the Southwest Regional final by a score of 71–61. It was the Rams' first trip to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Final_Four" title="Final Four">Final Four</a>. Against <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Butler_Bulldogs_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 Butler Bulldogs men's basketball team">Butler</a> in the Final Four, VCU lost 70–62. The <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_VCU_Rams_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 VCU Rams men's basketball team">2010–11 VCU Rams men's basketball team</a> finished 6th in the ESPN/USA Today Coaches Poll at the end of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> This was the highest ranking in VCU's history and the highest ranking of any team from the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Athletic_Association" title="Colonial Athletic Association">CAA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="VCU_Rams_women's_basketball"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="VCU_Rams_women.27s_basketball">VCU Rams women's basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: VCU Rams women's basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Former WNBA player and Notre Dame's all-time leading scorer Beth Cunningham coaches the VCU Rams women's team.</p>
<p>The VCU Rams Women's team enjoyed the most successful season in their history in the 2008–2009 season. The team finished the season with a mark of 26–7 overall and a 15–3 conference record. Notably the team was a perfect 16–0 at home. After finishing second in their conference the team headed to their first ever NCAA tournament game as the 10th seed, where the No. 7 seeded Rutgers eliminated them 57–51 on their home court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> In the 2009–2010 season Cunningham led the Rams to the NIT Sweet Sixteen where they were eliminated by Syracuse.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivals">Rivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Rivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rowdy_Rams.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="308" data-file-width="603" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Rowdy_Rams.jpg/350px-Rowdy_Rams.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Rowdy_Rams.jpg/525px-Rowdy_Rams.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4f/Rowdy_Rams.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rowdy_Rams.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rowdy Rams (far back) spelling out "VIRGINIA COMMONWEALTH!"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>VCU's main rival is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Dominion_Monarchs" title="Old Dominion Monarchs">Old Dominion University</a>. The "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VCU-ODU_basketball_rivalry" title="VCU-ODU basketball rivalry">VCU-ODU basketball rivalry</a>" is often regarded as the best college basketball rivalry in the Commonwealth of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The Rams' intra-city rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Spiders" title="Richmond Spiders">University of Richmond</a> ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_%26_Blue_Classic" title="Black &amp; Blue Classic">Black &amp; Blue Classic</a>"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> is bound to heat up now that the two schools are playing in the same conference again for the first time since 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rowdy_Rams">Rowdy Rams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Rowdy Rams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Rowdy Rams is a student-run athletic support organization that focuses on VCU men's basketball, while also attending and supporting the university's 16 other varsity teams. The group began during the 2002–2003 basketball season when a group of VCU Pep Band members and other students began coordinating cheers together and taking road trips to away games. The following year, the Rowdy Rams procured funding from the SGA and sponsorship from VCU's Athletic Department, solidifying themselves as an official organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sites.google.com_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-sites.google.com-149">[149]</a></sup> The Rowdy Rams offer members priority seating to all VCU men's basketball home games, a discount card for local restaurants and businesses, a free T-shirt, and free bus trips to road games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2011, The Rowdy Rams followed the men's basketball team to Houston for the Final Four. Despite the team's upset by Butler University, the fan organization never regretted their trip. "Our Rowdy Rams came here in full force; the spirit was on the court; you could feel it all around the arena."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2013, The Rowdy Rams won the annual Naismith Student Section of the Year award, which awards the most passionate student section in college basketball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia_Commonwealth_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Virginia_Commonwealth_University_alumni" title="List of Virginia Commonwealth University alumni">List of Virginia Commonwealth University alumni</a></div>
<p>VCU has a total of 182,746 alumni with 60,534 alumni living in the Richmond Metro Area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
